text:
I was given this recipe for a semester-long class assignment in which I had to alter the recipe to have 33% less sodium, 33% less calories, and replace the white rice with a whole grain.  I did this over 5 weeks, with a different test substitution.  The successful substitutions included: brown rice, elimination of the mushroom soup and using a whole can of Campbell's healthy request chicken soup, reducing the cheese by one cup and using a 75% reduced fat cheddar cheese instead of the two types of cheese.  The dish continued to be the favorite of the class after each substitution.  Hope everyone tries these easy substitutions!

Here's what I've done to make this recipe simpler.  I put the chicken in the skillet with the onion and brown them both.  I add the salsa and soups to the chicken and simmer till chicken is done.  I make rice as normal.  I mix the cheses right on the wax paper or parchment paper I shred it on.  I layer as directed.  Saves some pots!

text:
This is a great base recipe, but quite bland as written.  I am rating this 3 stars based on modifcations to boost the flavor.  HELPFUL HINTS:  Saute your chicken with chicken taco seasonings and the chopped onion, set aside.  Use prepared brown or spanish rice vs white rice.  Added one can of minced ortega chilis, 1 tsp of minced garlic (such as Spice World) and 1 tsp of cumin to the soup (used healthy request/low sodium soup) mixture and then proceded to follow the directions.  Substituted 1 cup of the Montery Jack for Pepper Jack cheese for an extra flavor boost.  DEFINITELY much more flavorful!

text:
I only made two changes to this recipe, the first was I used a can of rotel instead of salsa and the second was that I mixed the rice and soup mixture together before layering.  I put this together in the morning and than baked it in the afternoon, I covered it with reynolds non-stick foil and cooked it for 30 minutes removing the foil and baking for the last 10 minutes this keeps the cheese moist and stringy instead of crusty
My whole family enjoyed this and it was even good the next day as leftovers in my husbands lunch This recipe is very adaptable you can make it as spicy your family likes.  Thanks so much for posting this recipe.

text:
This was pretty darn good! My husband even liked it, and he is the pickiest in the family. I did tweak it a little bit, but stuck to the basics: I sauteed the onion along with some bell pepper, celery, and minced garlic.  Instead of doing the alternating layers, I put all of the rice in first, then the chicken, then the soup mixture, then the cheese. I also didn't use as much cheese as the recipe called for - I only used about a cup at the most. I took another reviewer's advice and covered it with foil for the first 30 minutes then uncovered for the remaining 10 minutes. It turned out great, with a bit of sour cream on top. I think I will make this again, and maybe add a can of corn and possibly some black beans. I also agree with another review that said this would be good as a filler for burritos.  I think I'll try that today for lunch.  :) Thanks so much for sharing!

text:
This tasted really good.  It is very similar to my mom's ckn & rice cass. except she doesn't use salsa.  I made a couple of changes in order for this to work for me.  First, I like to cook my chicken with flavor so I seasoned it with salt pepper and garlic powder.I then mixed the soups and rotel (didn't have salsa).  I used this mixture instead of water to cook my chicken.  I cooked it on medium stirring frequently so the mixture wouldn't scorch on the bottom.  I removed the chicken and diced.  I mixed all the rice and soup mixture together and then added the chicken.  I topped it with cheese (I reduced the amount to save a few calories) and popped it into the oven.  By the way, this recipe makes a ton.  We will be having this for lunch today and dinner tonight.

text:
HELPFUL TIPS: You can obviously use 2 can of cream of chicken OR mushroom if you're out of one.  Don't stress over amount of cheese.  Use enough to cover a layer in the middle and a layer on top.  If you're in a hurry, use tyson chicken and just cube (~3.5-4 cups).  If you use breasts, I just cube FIRST then put in skillet (with a little oil) for 12-14 min.  Always done, and then you don't have to wait for it to cool to cube.  I then mix in the same chicken skillet the salsa and soups.  Usually I use less chicken in recipes, but I'm glad I didn't w/this.  I am SO GLAD I didn't listen to the review about using less rice!!!!  It was the PERFECT amount to layer very thinly one layer on bottom and then middle.  Can't imagine using even a tiny less esp. if you're using the entire soup/chicken mixture (and why wouldn't you) ;)  BTW, I Spread out the rice with ...yes, my hands as it's the easiest. You REALLY should cover this with foil so it doesn't dry out.  I actually had to use my hand to push the casserole down a bit so the cheese wouldn't touch the foil and also had to foil more of a dome with the foil for the same reason.  It makes a lot which is good.  Leftovers are great in a busy house!  This is a great recipe to make ahead, put in fridge, and bake later.

text:
I loved this recipe and it was fantastic on a cold rainy day! I actually made this in the crock pot, because I have a crazy schedule. For me, cooking a little at a time works best. So I put 4 frozen chicken breasts in the crock pot with the salsa and onions and cooked on high for about 3 1/2- 4 hrs. I cooked brown rice in the rice cooker and after the chicken was very tender I pulled it apart with a fork, added the soups and half the cheese called for. I actually used Shredded 2% mild cheddar. I let that cook on low for about another hour, stirred in the rice and served with tortillas on the side. It was fabulous! My kids and fiancee raved about this one

I used some of the suggestions for adding more flavor, hot pepper cheese, seasoning chicken & cooking with onions.  I dislike cream of mushroom so I went the cream of chicken route & some low fat sour cream.  My other trick, on Sundays I get my rice cooker out & make 2-3 pots of rice.  I LOVE white rice, sorry not giving it up.  Serve it with fish, fried rice with chicken, it is a great side.  I then package the rice in serving size freezer bags & freeze.  During the week I pop it in the microwave in a glass casserole with lid & I am read to go.  I like to cook, but hate it when it is a chore.  I also cook my hamburger & freeze.  Then I can thaw & season & go.

text:
This was a simple, great recipe, comprised of ingredients that are usually on hand!  I did make a few changes...1) Cubed raw chicken and cooked in a skillet with the onion, added salt, pepper and garlic powder. 2) Mixed the soup with cheese, rice, and salsa...added a packet of taco seasoning. 3) Mixed the chicken/onion mixture with the soup mixture, then poured into casserole (i.e. No layering - just mixed it all together) 4) Topped with cheese and baked covered with foil for 30 minutes, 10 minutes uncovered.

text:
Salsa Chicken Rice Casserole Haiku: "Pretty tasty meal. I changed a couple small things, but liked it alot." I halved the recipe, using only 1 can of cream of chicken soup, that I'd mixed w/ the salsa, and a heavy sprinkle of "taco seasoning I" from AR, along with the onions that I'd lightly sauteed, b/c I didn't want them raw. I had leftover shredded chicken, so that saved me the effort of boiling and chopping the chicken breast. Layered and baked it as written, and my only complaint was that I think there was too much rice, and the recipe could maybe benefit from some additional ingredients, like black beans, corn, or squash. Otherwise, it was fun to put it together, though it didn't scoop out onto my plate looking as nice as it did in the baking dish, but appearances aside, tasted pretty darn good.

text:
***As written, this recipe is a 3 b/c it's Bland. W/ my modifications, it's a 4. *Sauteed onion w/ chicken and seasoned it with my own "taco seasoning". (I used 3 boneless chicken breasts)
*Reserved about less than 1/2 cup of the chicken broth and poured it in w/ the chicken & onion. 
*I used 1/2 cup of monterey cheese & 1/2 cup of cheddar, mixed it w/ 1 can of cream of chicken soup, then add it to the chicken.
*I steamed the brown rice(I use 1 cup), but added 1 TBS of chicken bouillon in the water. 
*After the rice is done, I add it to the chicken mixture, then mix in 1 cup of my homemade salsa verde, add more seasoning if needed, MIX EVERYTHING WELL, then pour the whole thing into the foiled casserole dish. (easy clean up)
*Cover w/ foil for 30MINS and then leave it off for the remaining 10MINS. 
*I let it set for at least 20MINS, then eat! MMMMM!

text:
I had to make several adjustments for this to be good for my family.  Plain, poached chicken is extremely bland so I cubed it before cooking and then sauteed it with salt, and onion and garlic powder.  Then fat and calories in this is too much to take so I just used the 98% fat free soups and no one can tell the difference.  I layered as directed but the onion on the top layer doesn't cook through.  The rest of the casserole is cooked through and then there are these odd pieces of raw onion.  I hate raw onion so I had to cover with foil and baked nearly twice as long as the recipe instructs.  End result was good but will definitly finely dice the onion, saute the chicken, continue using the low-fat soup, and cover the dish while baking next time.

text:
Used canned and frozen grilled chicken strips. While rice was cooking (1 cup) I sauteed half a large yellow onion and 4 minced garlic cloves in olive oil. Then added 2 handfuls of frozen grilled chicken strips. Let those warm up a bit and sprinkled a little chile powder, garlic salt, and pepper over them. Added mild and medium salsa (1 cup each) to the same pan. Stirred and added both soups. Then added one 12.5 oz can of chicken (which was perfect because there was chicken in every bite). Mixed in cooked rice and spread in  9x13 greased glass pan. Sprinkled Mexican Cheddar Jack cheese and Mozzarella cheese when half the mixture was in dish. Put rest of chicken mix in then topped with remaining 2 cups of cheese. Baked uncovered about 15 min. Turned out very yummy. Has a little kick but not enough to scare off my kids. Would be great with a side iceberg salad. I could see this being a hit as a potluck dish.

text:
This casserole is easy and AMAZING! Flavor balance is awesome....it's just great. It's totally great if you follow the recipe to the "t"; the only thing I changed was using 3c reduced fat cheddar cheese to cut the calories a little & upped the salsa by 1/2 c. I might make a little more rice next time, but that's a personal preference. Also, if you like a little kick, use a medium salsa instead of mild.
****UPDATE****: I've made this dish several times & have experimented & served to multiple people & have additional notes: To really cut the fat & cal but not the taste, use 98% fat free cr. of chicken & mushroom soups & 2 1/2-3c reduced fat cheddar cheese. This makes a HUGE nutritional impact & does not significantly affect taste!!! Also, you can cut the chicken by 30% with no impact to enjoying the dish & it FREEZES BEAUTIFULLY!!!

This recipe is delicious and incredibly easy to make!  We loved it so much, I made a second batch the day after I made the first!  I made it almost exactly as the recipe directed, with one exception being that I used Pepper Jack cheese (rather than Monterey Jack), since I had it on hand. The second time I made the recipe, I made a couple other substitutions, just to use up some other items in my pantry.  I used 2 cans of Cream of Celery soup (in place of the Cream of Mushroom and Cream of Chicken that the recipe suggests.)  I also used exclusively cheddar cheese, since I had a lot in the fridge.  It turned out well even with those changes. When I make this again, I'll use Pepper Jack and Cheddar; that really povided nice flavor, color and texture!

I made this recipe last night with left over Turkey from Thanksgiving.  I did change it up a bit.  Instead of using soup, I used white cheese queso.  I also added diced green chilis.  Also as many of the reviews suggested I mixed the rice, turkey and sauce together. I think the queso made a big difference because it had so much seasoning to it alone.  My husband really liked it and he isn't a caserole person.  I think had I not used the queso and added the chilis it would have been really lacking on the flavor as many people had said.

Pretty Good.  Decreased cooking time a lot by sauteing onion in pan 2 min, then adding cubed raw chicken and cooking till chicken no longer pink and onion opague.  Seasoned Chicken with Onion, Garlic & Chili Powder as well as black pepper.  Added can of soup and salsa to skillet, stirred till well blended then mixed in cooked rice.  Layered bottom of pan with Tortilla Chips, then mixture then cheese.  Would also be good with chips on top of mixture, underneath cheese.  Baked at 350 for 20 min.  Cut this recipe in half (family of 4 with two kids under 6).  Used 2 Chicken breasts, 3/4 cup rice (cooked in 1 1/2cup water), 1 can cream of chicken & mushroom soup 1 small onion, 3/4 - 1 cup salsa.  1 cup cheese. Baked in 8x8 casserole dish.  next time would add black beans (rinsed and drained) to mixture.  Could also add corn & diced red pepper (would saute with the onion).

text:
This was really good. I altered it a little based on our personal tastes and what I had in the pantry. There were only two of us so I mad 3 servings. I used 1 cooked chicken breast, cubed and mixed it with a can of black beans. The beans were a fantastic addition and made it a little more interesting than just with chicken. I used one can of low fat/sodium cream of chicken soup, 3/4c salsa, 1/4 chopped onion (raw), and 1/2 can chopped green chiles. Oh, also, for the rice, I had on of those 90 second microwave pouches of mexican rice which added some more depth than just regular white rice would have. Also, the cheese I used was a pre-packaged mexican blend and I barely used enough to cover each layer and it was more than enough.  I think the whole thing took me 5 minutes of prep work. Fantastic dish! Oooo, we had it with tortilla chips which made it even yummier!

text:
With a few minor changes I will put this in heavy rotation. I opted to dice, season & saut the chicken with the onions. For the rice I used 2 cups of the 5-min Minute Maid rice and for more flavor I used 2 cups of chicken broth instead of water and microwave covered for 8 min.    Added the chicken and  of the ingredients & mixed in together then stared the layers as the recipe stated. Covered in the oven for 30 min or so then uncover for 15min to get it to brown (this way everything has time to soak up all the flavors and the cheese on top does not overcook) Let sit a few minutes to cool off. *Also note that for those that would like a little heat try hot salsa instead of mild  (I recommend chi-chis)

This was very good. The only adjustment I made was to only use cream of chicken - no cream of mushroom and also I separated the layers with a flat, soft tortilla shell. So I put one tortilla shell in the bottom of my round baking dish, did one layer of rice, chicken, sauce, cheese; then I laid out another tortilla and then a second layering of ingredients. This gave the casserole some structure, so that when I cut pieces they actually stood and didn't get mushy and soupy. It also added one more flavor and texture - really tasty. Will defintely make again.

This was quite a big hit in my family.  I used hot, southwest style salsa, and I'm glad I did.  Without it, I'm afraid it may have been too bland.  (For the record, I never use hot salsa because I'm a wimp, but could not even tell it was hot in this dish.)  I diced the chicken and then cooked in oil in frying pan before adding to the casserole.  The only thing I will do differently next time is to season the chicken first; it could have used some fuego spice mix or, at the very least, some salt and pepper.  When I got a bite of it in the casserole, it didn't taste like much.  Overall, this was really yummy.  I will make it again.

text:
My husband said, "This is killer." I don't get that reaction with every casserole. :)
I made a few changes: 1) I omitted the cream of chicken soup (kinda grosses me out) and substituted a can of creamed corn for it, (slightly drained). 2) I added a diced red pepper, which added flavor, color and nutrition. 3) I used one large bone-in, skin-on chicken breast, broiled in water for 40 minutes (any less, and it won't be cooked through) and shredded that, then added it to some leftover taco-seasoned shredded pork loin and black beans mixture. 4) Ate it with Fritos sprinkled on top. Made altogether, this was spicy, flavorful, and a "killer" keeper. :) Thanks for the recipe!

text:
I mixed everything together and then put it in the casserole dish. I wanted a little more flavor, so I cooked the chicken breasts in salted water and used rice with Mexican seasoning (garlic powder, onion powder, chili powder, and chicken boullion powder) and added about 1 TBSP chili powder to the casserole. I left out the onion and used only cheddar cheese. I added a few handfuls of coarsely crushed tortilla chips to give the casserole a little more structure. I stuck the casserole in the microwave for about 6 minutes and served with refried beans. My husband and kids liked it, so it's a keeper. Thanks for sharing!

Here are the changes on made based on what I had on hand.  First I used yellow Spanish rice which really gave it great flavor.  I didn't have cream of mushroom so I substituted with 1 cup of sour cream, I added a can of drained rotel and only used 3/4 cup salsa.  I also sauteed my chicken with the onion and salt & pepper.  I also added a can of sweet corn which I really loved, it was a nice contrast with the spicy flavors and added some texture.  I didn't layer for time sake but combined everything together including 1/2 cup of cheese and them topped with remaining cheese (I also used pepper jack cheese on half for me and my hubby, would have been too spicy for the kids) cover with foil and cooked 30 min, uncovered and cooked an additional 10 minutes.  Very good will make again and will freeze half to have a quick meal on hand at a later date.

text:
Wow I can't believe how good this turned out, for how easy it was!  Took me about 10min to prep, and 35min to cook/bake: EASY!  The chicken was super moist, and my husband loved it with his Frank's hot sauce and a glass of cold beer. I did make some changes.  First I cut the recipe in half and used a 9x9 bake pan lined in foil b'cuz I cook for only 2 ppl here; I also used a rice cooker instead of using the stovetop.  In terms of ingredients, I used just 1 can of cream of chicken, medium Tostitos salsa, and shredded cheddar cheese. I used thawed frozen chicken breasts (I always have a bag in the freezer specifically for casseroles), and I let it marinate in Lawry's season-all and garlic powder while I chopped the onions. I tossed the chicken in a fry pan with oil on medium heat until done, then I tossed in the onions and simmered everything in some chicken broth. After about 8min, I layered as directed, but only made 1 layer. I covered the pan in foil, baked it for 20min, uncovered the pan and baked for another 5min. DELICIOUS! Will definitely be saving this recipe!

text:
I made this tonight and it was really good!  I usually try to make a recipe as is before I change things, but 1) I was lacking time and 2) I felt it needed more substance just from the list of ingredients.  So the changes I made are: I didn't see how 1 1/3 cup rice was enough for a 9x13 pan.  I made 1 1/3 at first but when I put half in the bottom, it barely covered the pan.  So while I was layering stuff, I made another 1 1/3 cup of rice.  I did use brown rice.  I bought Tyson precooked "diced ROASTED chicken" in the freezer section.  It's new.  I thawed that in the microwave and cooked in 1Tbsp olive oil along with the diced onion.  I added a can of fire roasted diced tomatoes to the chicken and simmered.  I bought healthy request cream soups to cut the sodium, bought "Pace FIRE roasted salsa" that had fire roasted peppers/corn in it.  Added a can of drained black beans to give it more body.  Mixed all of that together.  Layered the rice, then the chicken/tomato mixture, 2 cups cheese (bought Kraft 2% natural cheddar/mont jack), repeated.  Baked 30 minutes added the last layer of cheese last 10 min.  Served with corn bread....everyone loved it!  Had great flavor!  Think the fire roasted stuff really helped with that :)

text:
I have to say first that I didn't follow this recipe exactly as written.  I modified it because it looked like it would be very bland as written.  That said, here is what I did: I first boiled my chicken in water seasoned with PC Mexican Seasoning.  I then removed the chicken and used that water to boil my rice in.  I mixed together the cream of chicken, cream of mushroom, Rotel (instead or salsa), cheese, the chicken-chopped, and about another tablespoon of PC Mexican Seasoning.  To bake, I layered half the mixture on bottom, then the rice, then the rest of the mixture with cheese on top.  With adding the seasoning it was edible, but still bland.

text:
I changed this recipe quite a bit and it was really good.  I used instant brown rice instead of regular white rice and used 2 cups rice and 2 cups water.  I only used 2 cups of shredded cheddar instead of the additional 2 cups of mont. Jack to save some fat.  I used reduced fat cream of chicken & mushroom soups.  I added one can of kidney beans- drained and sprinkled half the kidney beans over the rice layers.  I was shocked that this recipe had NO spices so I added S&P, cumin, chili powder, and Johnny's Garlic seasoning to the soup mixture.  I also added a diced green onion to the soup mixture as well.  I added taco seasoning to the chicken after dicing it.  I served it with sour cream & green onions.  It was VERY tasty and FULL of flavor.  I would suggest adding some spices if you're going to try this recipe, I'm not sure it would have been as flavorful had I not done that.  My husband gave it a thumbs up as a keeper!  I gave it 4 stars since I did have to change it quite a bit, but the base recipe was great!

Our large family (14 of us) love this recipe.. i have made it several different ways and its wonderful the original way but we also enjoy variety. on other occasions i have substituted picante instead of salsa with colby jack cheese and cheddar  and have also added chipolte habeneros or jalepenos just under the top layer of cheese. It consistantly gets great raves and i have found that you can also use frozen precooked grilled chicken breast already chopped up, or rotissier chicken deboned to make it faster to prepare. i have made it with ground turkey seasoned with taco seasonings. i top it off with sour cream when serving and it has become the new family favorite having it at least two to three times a month in one of its many variations. thank you so much for this recipe. you turned whats for dinner into a question i dont mind answering!

text:
Totally Yummy!!! Based on some of the other reviews, here are the changes that I made:  1. Used 1.5 cups of uncooked brown rice (cook as directed before adding to casserole) 2. Used drained can of Rotel in place of the salsa 3. Instead of layering, I mixed everything up and then placed in pan and sprinkled the top with cheese. 4. Used less cheese.  I used 1 cup in the mixture and then just enough to cover the top of the casserole. 5. Added 1/2 cup of sour cream to mixture. 6. Gave the mixture a generous sprinkling of chili powder, cumin, and garlic powder 7. Sauteed some garlic with the onion 8. Added in a can of rinsed black beans  These changes made for a delicious dinner! Both kids, husband, and father-in-law loved it!!!

I have to admit that I had a bad feeling about trying this recipe.  My husband isn't usually a fan of casserole type dishes.  I had all the ingredients and it sounded good to me so I gave it a try.  Boy was I pleasantly surprised!  The hubs gave his approval, going back for seconds, and even had leftovers today in a burrito.  There was quite a bit of prep involved with cooking the rice and the chicken, mixing the sauce, assembling it all, etc but it was worth it.  I subbed rotel since that's what I had and we both really liked the flavor.  I also sauteed two cut up chicken breasts with the onion in a little bit of chili powder, garlic powder and cumin.  I added a can of black beans and some frozen corn too.  Topped with sour cream and with tortilla chips on the side, it made a great meal in our house that I'll make frequently.

text:
Delicious recipe, after reading other reviews I made a couple changes. I shredded the chicken instead of leaving it in cubes so it would be spread out more evenly, and I added seasoning to the chicken and boiled in chicken broth instead of water for more flavor. I made the rice as directed, but next time I will just make the rice like normal. The rice was a bit sticky this way and some stuck to the bottom of the pan. We used minute rice, and I did not cut back on the rice. I had a bit of trouble getting my son to eat it because of the salsa, I think I will put it in the food processor next time to make the chunks smaller. All of the adults approved. Very tasty, will definitely make again.

I didn't 'change' anything, except to cut the recipe in half because there's only two of us. I did add a can of black beans and a bit of leftover frozen corn to bulk it up a little. I also used green salsa (recipe doesn't specify what salsa to use). I know the recipe would be tasty as is, but I will say that with the additions, it was AWESOME. Hubs went back for seconds. I also cheated and did it the dump way. Just dumped all the ingredients into a bowl, raw rice and chicken and all, mixed and poured it into the baking dish. Covered it tightly with foil and baked for 30 minutes. Then took off the foil, covered with extra cheese and baked for an additional 20 minutes. This is going in our regular dinner rotation.

text:
First, and most important, POACH the chicken breasts, don't just plunk them down in water and boil.  That way you will get dry, stringy and flavorless chicken!  Put the chicken in a pot and cover with water,heat at med-high. When the water comes to a boil, reduce the heat to low, cover the pot, and let the chicken simmer VERY gently. Begin checking the chicken after 8 minutes: it is done when opaque through the middle and an instant-read thermometer in the thickest part of the meat registers 165F. Chicken is finished cooking in 10 to 14 minutes depending on the thickness of the meat and whether it is has a bone.  Also, put some aromatics in the  water; celery, any green herbs, such as parsley, sage, and a little salt. Then you can use that recipe!

I don't agree at all with the reviews that said it was bland  - just use a salsa with more kick or a different brand altogether.  I have made this a quite a few times. I have used different brands each time & I do prefer it made with certain salsas such as Jack's or Tostitos.  All my super picky ones ate this, had seconds and even told me how good it was. I also sauted the onion in butter to make it more tender.  I use Basmati rice which I prefer over plain white in this recipe.

text:
Yummy!  I halved the recipe and made a few changes as others suggested (mostly preparation not to the ingredients). I sauted the onions and chicken and added a can of red kidney beans (drained) to the rice. I mixed one can of cream of chicken soup with medium spicy chunky salsa. I layered 1/2 of the rice/bean mixture, 1/2 of the chicken/onion mixture, 1/2 of the soup and salsa mixture, and 1/2 of the cheese mixture in the prepared dish then repeated the layers, ending with cheese. I covered the casserole with foil and baked it for 30 minutes, removed the foil and baked for 10 more minutes. This dish was tasty and easy to prepare. I will definitely make it again!

Delicious! I did make changes with the help of a few other reviews & I added a few time savers.  Every weekend I roast a chicken to use for several dishes for lunch & dinner- chicken salad, tetrazzini, etc. So I used already roasted chicken & just sauteed with low sodium taco seasoning (but tempted to try without to see if that's necessary). I used 1.5 boil in a bag brown rices. I used the Campbell Select soups for lower sodium and only used 3 cups of cheese (but am thinking of trying only 2 cups next time- was very rich and cheesy). The next day we had it for lunch in whole wheat wraps!  I also may try it next time adding corn and black or refried beans- think it would add something.  Thanks for the recipe!

Following some of the suggestions I made the following changes;
For 8
1 cup brown rice
2 cups light Mexican cheese
1 can healthy request chicken soup
3/4 can low sodium Mushroom soup
1 1/4 cup medium salsa

Brown the chicken and onion and drain some of the liquid before adding the soups and salsa. 
Layer as instructed.
Family raved about the flavor and will definitely make it again.

This is an excellent base recipe. I only gave it 4 stars because I did change several things based on what I had on hand...so this is what I did and it was so yummy! I had a box of Zatarains Dirty Rice mix I used that instead of the rice. I cooked the chicken with diced onion and bell pepper, added a can of pinto beans and seasoned with Cajun Seasoning. The seasoning from the rice box worked so well for this and made the salsa flavor unnecessary, my hubby loved this and he doesn't usually care for casseroles.

text:
I made this last night for dinner and it was definitely tasty but, as others have suggested, a few additions can help. Also, I used leftover turkey (about 2 cups of chopped for 4 servings) instead of fresh chicken. 
Other changes I made included: using brown Basmati rice; adding about 2 TBSP of chopped green onions to the salsa (and reducing the chopped white onion by about the same amount); reducing the amount of cheese by 50%; adding salt, pepper and a dash of Taco seasoning; and adding a layer of Tostito round tortilla chips on the top just before the final cheese layer. 
I will certainly make this again as a little change from my usual Chicken/Rice/Broccoli concoctions.

text:
Great recipe! There's a lot of prep work for this recipe, but well worth taking the time to make it. To make life easier, I would suggest cooking the rice and chicken the night before so that the only thing left to do the day you want to make it is to layer it and bake it  (particularly if you are coming home from work). I made a change to the onions - I microwaved them for 1 min to make sure they would be cooked all the way through in the casserole. Also, I have a hard time making any casserole without vegetables. It just seems wrong. So I chopped up 1/2 green pepper, 1 red pepper, and 4 oz of fresh mushrooms, microwaved them for 1 min and added them with the chicken. It was soooo good!

text:
We make this all the time, it goes a long ways.  My family eats it as a burrito though.  I also make it easier by doing it in two pans.  One I cook the rice in.  The second I cook the rest in a skillet.  I cube the chicken into bite sized pieces and brown them and cook them the rest of the way in the soup and salsa mixture.  (I only use the one can of cream of chicken, no more is needed)  It doesnt need all of the cheese either.  I dont even add the cheese to the mixture.  Add the cooked rice to the chicken and soup mixture.  Put some of the mixture on a flour tortilla, add some cheese and fold it up.  Sometimes we fry the burrito in oil and serve it with sour cream...yummy and easy

Totally easy to make, I had some frozen chicken thighs threw thse bad boys into a pot to de thaw, seasoned them up with some sazon, salt pepper, squeezed out some fresh garllic, and chopped up some onion, for about 20 minutes, while tat was cooking, mixed up the salsa, and the sour cream,  ( didn't have the cream of anything soup) added a can of corn,some chives and some more seasoning, mixed it up and added some more shredded cheese to it. -- Nuked some basmati rice 20 minutes and --due to time restraints I just sprayed pam on the bottom of the glass dish layer of rice-- Chicken on top Creamy mixture, Layered Some cheddar chese ( again had noting else) and a sprinkle of Mustard powder on top -- Cooked for about 45 minutes on 350--- It as perfect. this is a very versitile recipe. text:
Delicious!  I made this last night and am munching on it for lunch today.  This is an excellent casserole!  For mine, I used 1 cup of brown rice, 3 chicken breasts, and added a cup of black beans and also a can of corn.  As other reviewers suggested, I browned the chicken a bit in olive oil and crushed garlic, then added some salsa for the breasts to cook in before adding the soups directly into the pot to simmer.  Used onion powder instead of onions (personal preference), and added a little taco seasoning to the simmering chicken-soup mixture.  Used approximately 14 oz. of salsa.  Since most of the Mexican cheeses were already eaten, I added in Farmer's cheese (what I had on hand), which worked well.    Layering wasn't necessary. This tastes great alone or served with tortilla chips. :)

text:
To make this dish more flavorful, I did several things: First, I added garlic and onion to the rice as it was cooking.  I cut the chicken breasts into 3 or 4 pieces each. Then, I sauteed onion, garlic and green pepper in a little olive oil and added the chicken on top of that to cook almost all the way. On both sides of the chicken, I sprinkled cumin and ground red pepper (cayenne).  Finally, I used medium salsa (Jack's Special- Costco).  This dish was very flavorful, quite spicy and delicious!  I will make it again!

Next time I will try all salsa instead of substituting the rotel.

For perfect, nearly sticky rice (my fav!) for every 1 cup of rice add 1.5 cups of water, bring to a boil, cover & simmer for 20 minutes. Perfect every time! Anyway, I took the advice in one of the reviews to add extra salsa... Oops! Big mistake on my part. I went a little salsa crazy & all I could taste was the salsa! I simmered the chicken in the sauce on the stovetop & I mixed the rice & chicken together. I think 2 cups of cheese is waaay too much, so I only used a handful of cheddar and broiled the casserole for 5 minutes before serving. Overall this is a good weeknight recipe.

text:
I love this recipe!  It is very good as-is. However, I need less calories than 588 so like most people I have adjusted it a bit.  I use brown rice instead of white - healthier and I thought it gave more flavor.  I use the cream of mushroom with garlic to add a little zing.  I look for reduced fat or sodium on all of the soups because that's alot of sodium in a serving.  I'm going to use reduced fat cheddar next time just to cut the calories back a bit.  We'll see since I don't think the reduced cheddar melts as nicely - if it doesn't I'll go back to normal cheddar.  Also, 1/8th of the recipe is huge with all of the layers involved and so this lasted a few days more than expected - which was A-OK with my family because they loved it!!

Ive been on a Sunday casserole kick lately in order to give us lunch through the week, and this one makes the cut. I made a couple of modifications...I used a rotisserie chicken (shredded), and I used medium salsa instead of mild. I mixed the soup mixture in with the chicken before spreading. It seemed to be lacking just a little bit of freshness, but Im not sure what else I would change to bring that to the dish...maybe top with lettuce & tomato. All in all, I think this one will be added to our Sunday casserole rotation.

text:
I gave this recipe 5 stars for it's versatility. My family likes heat with their Mexican food and I don't like anything spicy. As written, I thought the recipe looked to bland for us. Here are the changes I made. I used 2 packs of Knorr Spanish Rice. I used 2 cans of Kirkland brand chicken. I sauteed the chicken in olive oil along with onions and green peppers. I combined cream of chicken soup and the salsa and added that to the chicken mixture. Tossed in a can of drained black beans and fire roasted corn. Topped with crushed Doritos and Mexican style cheese. Covered with foil and baked 40 minutes. I omitted the sour cream because I'm lactose intolerant.  Hubby and kids added it to theirs. This recipe is a keeper. Thanks for sharing.

I cooked the chicken in olive oil with the onion, 1 tsp of minced garlic, and 1 tsp of cumin. I used 1 cup pepper jack cheese, 1/2 cheddar, 2 and 1/2 fiesta blend. I used a black bean and corn salsa mmh. I also used 2 cream of mushroom instead of chicken. Over all this was good. I also saw no need in layering all this separately. Once the chicken was done I added the other ingredients followed by the rice. I did layer with Cheese in the middle. My husband and son liked it which is saying a lot. I still thought it was slightly bland. I topped it off with a little salsa and sour cream which did the trick. Next time I make it I will tweak it a little more and either do more salsa or take out 1 can of soup. Im thinking take a can of soup out. Over all it is a good recipe!

text:
I am giving this recipe 4 stars because it is a good base recipe you can adjust to your family's preferences.  I halved it for our family of 4. Some changes I made are I used brown rice. .  I used a can of Rotel rather than the salsa and added some black beans.  I did liberally season the chicken with taco seasoning.   I  then  simply dumped everything together (except the cheese) in a casserole dish and baked it till the chicken was cooked (about an hour).  I then shredded/cut up the chicken, added the cheese, covered with foil, and continued baking  till the cheese was melted.

text:
This was a very filling dish. But the flavor was a bit bland and it had a very tangy after taste I didn't care for. I did make a few changes to the dish but not enough to not give a review.

I seasoned raw chicken breast with taco seasoning and cut it in strips and cooked until just a touch underdone. Then I cooked the diced onion in the same pan since I didn't want to risk the onions being undercooked as other reviewers noted. I cooked the rice in the soup mixture in the oven after assembling it all together. I mixed the soups and salsa, then the rice (plus 1/2-3/4 cup more since it didn't look like there'd be enough) and onion together then added 1 1/2 canfuls of water to help cook the rice. Pour the mixture over the chicken and cook on 425* for about 40-60 minutes covered depending on your rice.

text:
Too gooey - 
I found this very tasty, using the guidance of other reviewers and adding taco seasoning and onions to the browning chicken tenders, which i then mixed in to the other components whole.  The tenders are small strips and they add a little variety in the texture.  I also used Herr's Black Bean and Corn Salsa, which provided just the right - not too spicy - kick to the dish, with a slightly different salsa flavor.  However, i found the rice and soup mixture to be distractingly gooey.  And that is with a fair amount of onions that release moisture as they cook.  Next time i'll cut the condensed soups with some broth or water, and keep the total to 2 soup cans worth.

text:
With the changes I made following other reviews this was pretty good.   
1) I fried the chopped up chicken (bite-size pieces) with onion and sweet pepper. Added 1 tsp cumin and 1 tsp chili powder. Put aside to cool.
2) I cooked brown rice in chicken stock, about twice what the menu said.  
3) I used medium salsa.  
4) I cut the cheese in half.  
5) I used two cans of cream of chicken.  

My husband and son liked it and scarfed it and said it was a keeper.

I had to create an account just so I could review this recipe.  Everyone in my house loved it, and that is a very rare thing.  This will start in our regular rotation! I only made one ingredient change, and that was to use Cream of Celery instead of Cream of Chicken - I don't like Cream of Chicken.  I also made some prep changes to save time.  1. text:
I rated this a 3 star the first time we made, but now I'd give it a 4 with changes.  I would've just updated the other review, except with this format you can't find your own reviews that easy. That said if this recipe is a good starting point for you try others suggestions like adding black or kidney beans, cumin (we'd used 1/4 tsp but going to 1/2 tsp next time).  Adding green chilies was helpful also.  We usually use a mild salsa so had it been med or hot probably wouldn't use chilies.  We also decided after last nights meal that if using beans we won't use as much rice.  This is a keeper for sure now.  Very flexible to your own personal tastes.

Yummy! I did make some changes, however. I sauteed the onion with some chopped bell peppers (2) and half a jalapeno. I also sauteed the chicken in some olive oil and seasoned it with 1 tsp. each of cumin, oregano, adobo and garlic powder. I only used one can of cream of mushroom soup and a whole jar of salsa. I also added a can of drained and rinsed black beans. I would have thrown in a can of corn too, but I didn't have any. I used less cheese than called for too. I topped it all off with a can of enchilada sauce, a little cheddar and a small can of sliced black olives. Will definitely make this again. Maybe will try half rice/half quinoa next time.

text:
Made this today for a covered dish and loved it. I made these changes:
I sauted the onions in butter with a few cloves of garlic. Added 1 cup white rice , water and a teaspoon of chicken bullion to cook all.
I sprinkled cumin and chili powder over the chicken breasts, drizzled them with olive oil and roasted at 425 till just cooked thru. 
I tossed the cooked, chopped chicken breast with 1 can of the cream soup, Rotel in place of the salsa, and a finely chopped jalapeo pepper. 
I used only one layer of each-rice on the bottom, chicken/Rotel mixture next layer, sprinkled a can of black beans over the chicken mixture and covered it all with a nice layer of the grated cheese. 
After baking I sprinkled the top with chopped green onion and served with sour cream. Yummy!!

text:
I ended up using this as a base recipe and changed it up some.  First I sauteed the rice with about  1/2c of onions with a pinch of salt . I cut the chicken into bite size chunks, seasoned them with taco seasoning then cooked them with another 1/2c of onion. I added a bag of frozen corn and some leftover black beans, about 1 1/2c. I did not use the cans of soup. I layered the rice, corn, black beans, chicken, salsa, then cheese and baked it for 15 minutes.  After it was done I added a dollop of guacamole and some cilantro.  My children loved it.

Changes I made:  I cut up the raw chicken and cooked it with the onion (and added 3 cloves garlic to chicken and onion). text:
I'm about to be that person who gives a less than glowing review for a recipe she did not follow exactly. Apologies in advance; it wasn't bad, but it was very bland. I halved the recipe, omitted the cream of mushroom (half recipe only needed a half can of each, so I used a whole can of cream of chicken) used shredded cooked chicken I already had, mixed the soup, salsa & onions with the cooked rice before layering, subbed pepper jack for the monterey jack, and only baked for 20 minutes (everything was already cooked and it was plenty hot by then). Next time, would definitely add chili powder and cumin, and maybe a can of diced green chiles and some olives. I also thought there was too much cheese (and I LOVE cheese). I think I'd cut the cheese in half and only use it on top. Husband and I ate it dip-style with tortilla chips, which he liked. I usually have all of these ingredients on hand, so with a little doctoring, I can see us trying this again.

text:
This was a pretty easy recipe to make, but I made it as-written and agree with those who said that it was kind of bland. The boiled chicken and white rice fill out the baking dish but don't do much to enhance the final flavor. I think the concept is fine and I might try making the dish again with some modifications. Instead of boiling the chicken, I would suggest brushing it with oil and southwestern spices and roasting it in the oven. It's nearly as fast and easy as boiling and will yield a much nicer flavor and texture. I would also do what some others have suggested and use a Spanish or Mexican rice instead of plain white rice. (I also found that I had more rice than I needed with this recipe and had to leave some out so that I didn't overfill my baking dish.) I would also saut the chopped onion, along with a clove of minced garlic. And while I'm a big fan of cheese, I'd probably cut that back a bit too, maybe 3 cups total instead of 4, because it just seemed like a bit too much at the end.

I thought this recipe was really really good!  I followed the original recipe ALMOST exactly, but I think there are a few things that were necessary.  I used 2 cups monteray jack cheese, and 2 cups shredded Velveeta cheese.  This made the cheese flavor a little stronger, as my family loves the traditional salsa/velveeta queso dip.  I also cooked the chicken in a pan and added the onions to saute, and then shredded the chicken instead of cutting it into cubes.  I think you should at least have 1.5 lbs of chicken with this, because there's too much sauce witthout it.  Or a little more rice to thinken it up a bit.  But it really was great!!  It made a lot and we are looking forward to the leftovers!

text:
I only gave this a 3 because I had to make so many changes to fix how bland it was.  Instead of all salsa, I used a can of Rotel with diced green chilies and topped it up to the 1 1/2 cups with mild salsa. I also used both dark and light meat for better flavor.  Rather than layering, I mixed the cooked rice, both soups, onion and salsa together along with about 1 tsp salt and 1 tsp cumin.  Then I stirred in the chicken and half the cheese.  I sprinkled the remaining cheese over the top after pouring into the pan.  The cooking time is confusing.  In one place it says an hour and at the end it says 40 minutes.  I baked for 40 minutes, took off the foil and baked for another 20 to get the top all bubbly. I served it with homemade guacamole. Finally, this said 8 servings.  Since this fills the pan to the absolute top, this 9x13 ends up being 12 servings in our house.  Next time I'll cut the recipe in half and bake it in an 8x8 pan.  We had so much leftover that we ended up using it as a filling for burritos the next night.  With the remaining (yes, I still had more leftovers), I made up more burritos, and froze them flat on a cookie sheet.  After they were solid, I just put them all in a freezer bag.  My son heats them in the microwave (just like store bought frozen burritos) at work.

This was delicious! I read many of the recommendations in the comments and modified it accordingly. I used Kirsten's recommendations for making the recipe healthier, and I browned the chicken and onions in a skillet along with fajita sauce. It gave the chicken a lot of extra flavor. I used instant brown rice to save time, and it worked fine. I also used medium salsa, because my fiance likes spicier foods. The results were simply superb! I will definitely make this again, but next time I think I will use less onions and add corn and pinto beans.

text:
Okay, I modified this a lot to reduce fat. I rubbed the chicken breast with olive oil, salt, pepper, garlic powder and basil and then baked for 1 hour at 350. I also used brown rice and added 1 tsp of chicken boullion in the water while it was simmering. For the sauce, I used a can of 95% fat free cream of celery soup and 1 cup of boiling water with 1 tsp of chicken bouillon, chopped onion and 1 1/2 cup of green salsa since I was out of red salsa. I mixed the rice, sauce, chicken and 2 cups of 2% mild cheddar cheese together and baked.  It was very good. Try it with crushed tortilla chips for a different taste.

This was delicious.  I have to say I didn't make it according to the original post, but wow, my whole family just inhaled it.  I took the rice down to 1 cup and took the water down to 2 1/4.  I opted to cook this on the stove top. I added garlic and pepper.  I cut the chicken into chunks and sauted this in a tiny bit of olive oil with 1/4 tsp. cumin until it was almost brown and then added  1/2 chopped green pepper, 1/2 red pepper, 1/2 onion and 1/2 fresh mushroom.  I kept the original cheeses and the original amounts. I added the cream of mushroom and omitted the cream of chicken.  I just threw everything together in the 9 x 13 in dish and just stirred it all together.  I baked for 20 min at 350 degrees.  My kids even went nuts!! Thanks for sharing!! This would be great with almost any veggie combo. I'll be putting broccoli in next time and my children have requested this with peas!!

text:
UPDATE: MADE THIS AGAIN, FOLLOWING GWENETH'S COOKING DIRECTIONS TO THE LETTER THIS TIME (I.E. THE LAYERING STEPS). MADE THE SAME MODS AS LAST TIME, BUT USED FIESTA CORN INSTEAD, ADDED A PACKET OF CHICKEN TACO SEASONING TO MY MEAT AND SAUTED MY ONION TO SOFTEN IT. I ALSO USED LONG GRAIN RICE AND COOKED IT IN BROTH TO ADD FLAVOR. BAKED UNCOVERED THE ENTIRE TIME. YUM! This was "OK". It's a shame that my fiance and I didn't like this enough to eat any of the leftovers because this makes a TON!!! This recipe is pretty forgiving. Add anything you want - beans, veggies, etc. I pretty much followed Gweneth's directions but did make a few substitutions. I added a 15 oz. can of (drained) sweet corn and subbed a can of cream of chicken with herbs soup for the cream of mushroom called for. I also revised the amount and types of cheese I used based on what I had in my fridge. To speed prep, I shredded a Mexican-seasoned rotisserie chicken. My only other changes were to use Minute Rice and to follow the cooking instructions printed on the back of the box (i.e. equal parts rice / water). I mixed everything together (as opposed to layering as directed) in my baking dish, reserving HALF of my cheese for topping my casserole. Baking for 25 minutes covered / 15 uncovered worked well for me. Topping individual servings with pickled jalapeno slices and using Tostito's scoops for dipping was a nice touch. All in all, this was decent, but nothing I'm anxious to repeat. Thanks anyways, Gweneth. :-)

text:
I have made this twice now and my family loves it.  The first time I made it according to the recipe.  The second time I did alter it slightly with even better results.  I was pressed for time so I needed to combine a couple steps.  First, I used 2 cups minute rice (uncooked) and mixed it with the soup/salsa mixture (I added about 1/2 can of water to thin down the soups a little).  I chopped green onions to use instead of regular onion but I did not mix that with the soups.  I layered half the soup/rice mixture, chicken, gr. onion, then cheese, and repeated.  I baked this at 300 degrees F for about 2 hour.  We liked it better this way, the rice seemed to absorb the flavors more.  Thank you for posting this recipe.  I will definately be making this again.

This was surprisingly good. I did not have high hopes, but the whole family (even the very picky 5 year old) really liked it. It worked really well so this will be a great dinner for evenings when time is short or we need a meal that can cook unattended.

This was great!  Didn't change a thing.  I can see it being very good for variations, particularly in the soup.  I followed another reviewer's suggestions and cooked the onion, chicken, soups and salsa together to save on washing up!  Thanks. UPDATE:  I tried this in the slow cooker last night and it turned out great!  Follow the recipe but reserve some of the chicken mixture for the top then sprinkle with the cheese.  Set slow cooker to LOW and cook for about 7 hours.  Perfect!

country:

text:
I'm into easy, now that I cook for just me - so I made some changes, but still wound up with a yummy dinner for several nites!  To halve the recipe I did the following:  I sauteed a cicken breast and a turkey cutlet (all I had in the freezer) cut into bite size pieces while they were still partially frozen. Then, in the same pan, I sauteed 1/4 cup of green pepper, diced, 1/2 cup of diced onion and a tablespoon of minced garlic.  While I was doing this, I cooked, as per directions on the box, 1 packet of whole grain and wild rice. In a bowl, I mixed 1 can of cream of chicken soup, nearly 3/4 cup of medium salsa, the onion mixture, the rice and the chicken and turkey, and poured it into a casserole dish.  Then I mixed a cup of shredded mozzarella and 1 cup of shredded cheddar (again, all I had in the fridge) and sprinkled the cheese on top of the chicken and soup mix.  Cooked it covered for 30 minutes, then uncovered until the cheese was slightly brown.  SOOOOOOO good! Will do this often, and probably still using both the chicken and the turkey. It went together quickly, and , served with cornbread and some green beans, I couldn't have asked for anything better.

I thought it was ok...my husband really liked it. After making it, I thought that it might make a good burrito filling, as one reviewer mentioned.I did modify the recipe a bit by using chicken broth to cook the rice in to add more flavor, and while boiling the chicken, I added a little salt, basil, bay leaf, and peppercorns to flavor the water.I didn't have a can of cream of chicken so I used sour cream as a substitute...maybe this is why it turned out a little too "mushy" for my taste. text:
I decided to use this as a side dish to our chicken breasts that we grill. I put some olive oil in a pan and added chopped onion, chopped up peppers, garlic and one can of diced tomatoes with green chilis. I used garlic powder, salt and pepper for seasoning. I added the salsa mixture to my microwaved rice(directions on box)in the bowl that it was cooked in. Then I put just one can of cream of chicken soup and the cheese in the pan I had already been using and cooked till bubbly then added that to the salsa rice. It had some heat, but was so good, and the total cook time was under 30min because we grill our chicken on the side.

I made this recipe with a few variations (listed below) and felt a little like I was eating the filling to something.  So I paired it with refried beans in a large tortilla and it makes a fantastic burrito filling!  Wrap and toast lightly on both sides for a delicious and filling meal.

Changes from the original recipe:
I used 1 pouch of boil in bag rice to save time
I used a heaping tablespoon of light sour cream instead of cream of mushroom soup
I added 1/2 tsp cumin and 1 tsp chili powder for a little extra flavor

This is a wonderful recipe. Made it for the picky inlaws and they loved it! Definately a keeper. Subbed cream of celery soup for cream of mushroom due to allergies and still worked well.
